Jamison Brereton

23 (464)
Indra
Bharadv─Бja B─Бrhaspatya
10 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh
This hymn focuses on IndraтАЩs vital connection with soma and on the reciprocal relationship between the soma-presser and Indra, the soma-drinker. This theme is established in the first p─Бda of the first verse, and every subsequent verse has some reference to soma: all but verse 8 contain a form of the word so╠Бma (and vs. 8 does make clear reference to soma-induced exhilaration), and of those, all but verse 7 have тАЬpressed,тАЭ тАЬpressing,тАЭ or тАЬpresserтАЭ as well. The other ritual aspects of the soma sacrifice, especially the poetry and sacred formulations, also receive frequent men
tion. The reminders to Indra that sacrificial labor should be requited with gifts and help from the god occur throughout the hymn, but are not annoyingly obtrusive. Stylistically the hymn is noteworthy for its pairs of syntactically linked verses: 1тАУ2 with their тАЬor whenтАЭ clauses; 3тАУ4 with their run of agent nouns governing accusa tive objects; 5тАУ6 with a number of repeated formulae.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Indra For the repetitive lexicon and the unusual amount of linkage between vss., see published introduction.

рд╕реЛрдореЗ рд╕реБрддреЗ рдЗрддреН рдЕрднрд┐рд╖реБрдд рдПрд╡ рд╕рддрд┐ рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордгрд┐ рдмреГрд╣рддрд┐ рдорд╣рддрд┐ рд╕реНрддреЛрдореЗ рд╕реНрддреЛрддреНрд░реЗ рдЙрдЪреНрдЪрд╛рд░реНрдпрдорд╛рдгреЗ рд╕рддрд┐ рдЙрдХреНрдереЗ рд╢рд╕реНрддреНрд░реЗ рд╢рд╕реНрдпрдорд╛рдиреЗ рд╕рддрд┐ рд╣реЗ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ рддреНрд╡рдВ рдирд┐рдорд┐рд╢реНрд▓рдГ рдирд┐рдорд┐рд╢реНрд░рдГ рд╕рдиреН рд╣рд░реА рд╕рдВрдпреЛрдЬрдпрдиреН рд╣реЗ рдордШрд╡рдиреН рдзрдирд╡рдиреН рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ рддреНрд╡рдВ рдмрд╛рд╣реНрд╡реЛрдГ рд╣рд╕реНрддрдпреЛрдГ рд╡рдЬреНрд░рдВ рд╕реНрд╡рдХреАрдпрдорд╛рдпреБрдзрдВ рдмрд┐рднреНрд░рддреН рдзрд╛рд░рдпрдиреН рдпреБрдХреНрддрд╛рднреНрдпрд╛рдВ рд░рдереЗ рдирд┐рдпреБрдХреНрддрд╛рднреНрдпрд╛рдВ рд╣рд░рд┐рднреНрдпрд╛рдореН рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд╛рднреНрдпрд╛рдВ рдпрд╛рд╕рд┐ рдпрджреНрд╡рд╛ рдЖрдЧрдЪреНрдЫрд╕реАрддрд┐ рдпрдЪреНрдЪ рддрддреНрд╕реЛрдореЗрд╜рднрд┐рд╖реБрддреЗ рдЗрддрд┐ рд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзрдГ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIndra, when the Soma is being effused, the sacred hymn chanted, the prayer recited, be you prepared (to harness your horses), or, Maghavan, with your horses ready harnessed, come (hither), bearing the thunderbolt in your hand.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

You are intertwined in the pressed soma, Indra, and in the praise song, in the sacred formulation, and in solemn speech as it is recited,
when, bounteous one, you drive with your two yoked fallow bays,
bearing your mace in your arms,

Jamison Brereton Notes

The rendering of n├нmi┼Ыla- as тАШintertwinedтАЩ may be a bit over the top, but тАШattached toтАЩ or тАШlinked toтАЩ is too anodyne; assuming an underlying sense тАШmixedтАЩ, the point is that Indra canтАЩt be separated from the substances and words offered to him in the ritual.

The standard NP sut├й s├│me is polarized at the boundaries of p─Бda a, allowing s├│me to directly adjoin its rhyme form (and ritual partner) st├│me over the p─Бda boundary – a simple but effective use of word order.

On b├нbhrad v├бjram see comm. ad VI.20.9.

Griffith

THOU art attached to pressed-out Soma, Indra, at laud, at prayer, and when the hymn is chanted;
Or when with yoked Bays, Maghavan, thou comest, O Indra, bearing in thine arms the thunder.

Geldner

Am ausgepre├Яten Soma, am Loblied, am erbaulichen Wort, am aufgesagten Lobgedicht h├дngst du, Indra, ob du mit dem geschirrten Falbenpaar, die Keule in den Armen tragend, ausziehst, o gabenreicher Indra;

Grassmann

Du liebst, o Indra, ausgepressten Soma, Gebet und Loblied, hergesagte Spr├╝che, Wenn, m├дcht’ger, du mit den geschirrten F├╝chsen, o Indra, kommst, den Blitz im Arme tragend.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬOr as, although engaged in heaven in the hero-animating conflict with foes, you protect the offerer of the libation, and humblest, undaunted Indra, the Dasyus, the disturbers of the pious and terrified worshipper, (so do you come when the soma is effused.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

There is no verb in the text; ‘come’ is assumed from the previous с╣Ыca: so, the reading is: when the soma is poured forth

Jamison Brereton

Or when on the decisive day, Indra, you help the soma-presser in the smiting of obstacles [/Vr╠еtra] and at the contest of champions,
or when, (yourself) being unafraid, as their skill became fearful, you subdued the vaunting Dasyus, Indra.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The gen. phrase d├бkс╣гasya bibhy├║с╣гaс╕е is troublesome, as it is not clear who or what it refers to or what its syntactic function is. Oldenberg interpr. it as a тАЬdativischer Gen.,тАЭ though he gives no tr. But Geldner seems to take it as a gen. absolute: тАЬw├дhrend der Entschlossene Furcht hatte.тАЭ In either case d├бkс╣гa- seems to be taken as an adj.

qualifying a human and this fearful human is taken to be one on our side, aided either directly (datival gen.) or indirectly (gen. abs.) by fearless Indra. In this passage the single тАШskillfulтАЩ (or тАШdeterminedтАЩ: GeldnerтАЩs тАШentschlossenтАЩ) person would presumably be the soma-presser (s├║с╣гvi-) of ab, and this is not impossible. However, although there are a few undoubted exx. of adjectival d├бkс╣гa- тАШskillfulтАЩ (e.g., I.51.2 d├бkс╣г─Бsa с╣Ыbh├бvaс╕е), in most clear exx. the stem is a masc. abstract тАШskill, abillityтАЩ, and in doubtful cases I prefer to seek such a meaning. Here I suggest that the тАЬfearful skillтАЭ belongs to IndraтАЩs enemies, the d├бsy┼лn of d, and depicts their fading confidence in their skill or ability to counter Indra. Under this interpr. it can either be a gen. abs. with Geldner (though this construction is rare at any stage and is supposed not to exist before Vedic prose; see Delbr├╝ck, AIS 389-90) or is a gen. of quality (although this construction is also marginal) with d├бsy┼лn тАЬthe Dasyus of frightened skill.тАЭ The published

tr. represents an absolute interpr.; the gen. of quality might be a better analysis, but is difficult to render in Engl., as the tr. just given shows (better тАЬof daunted/craven skill,тАЭ but this would lose the etymological figure). (K├╝mmelтАЩs [336] tr. avoids the problem, but unfortunately only by an unusual grammatical lapse on his part: he explicitly identifies bibhy├║с╣гaс╕е as acc. pl., which it could be, but tr. the phrase d├бkс╣гasya bibhy├║с╣гaс╕е as a single NP [тАЬf├╝r den Geschickten die sich f├╝rchtendenтАЭ] apparently failing to remember that d├бkс╣гasya requires the whole phrase to be gen. sg.

He takes this supposed acc. pl. as parallel to ┼Ы├бrdhataс╕е, which he separates from d├бsy┼лn and takes as another qualifier of those aided by Indra. His full tr. is тАЬOder wenn du f├╝r den Geschickten die sich f├╝rchtenden furchtlos unterwarfst f├╝r den K├╝hnen, Indra, die Dasyus.тАЭ The misparsing of d├бkс╣гasya excludes this tr.)

Griffith

Or when on that decisive day thou holpest the presser of the juice at Vrtra’s slaughter;
Or when thou, while the strong one feared, undaunted, gavest to death, Indra, the daring Dasyus.

Geldner

Oder ob du am entscheidenden Tage dem Somabereiter beistehst, Indra, in dem Feindekampf um den Heldenpreis, oder als du selbst furchtlos, w├дhrend der Entschlossene Furcht hatte, die ├╝berm├дchtigen Dasyu┬┤s unterwarfst, Indra.

Grassmann

Und wenn dem Presser am Entscheidungstage, in Feindesschlacht beim Kampf du, Indra, beistehst, Wenn ohne Furcht du unterwarfst, o Indra, die frechen Feinde des erschreckten Dakscha.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay Indra be the drinker of the effused soma, he who is the fierce conductor of the worshipper to security; may he be the donor of the world to the presenter of the libation, the giver of wealth to the man who adores him.тАЭ

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay Indra, with his steeds, come o us as many (daily) rites (as may be celebrated), bearing the thundeerbolt, drinking the soma, bestowing cattle, granting manly and multiplied posterity, hearing the invocation of his adorer, and being the accenter of (our) praises.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Going to even such pressings as these with his two fallow bays, bearing his mace, drinking soma, giving cows,
who makes the manly hero possessed of hale heroes, the hearer of the singerтАЩs call, for praise songs are his vehicle. с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes

The alternation of root-accented -tar- agent nouns and redupl. agentive - i-stems, both with verbal rection, is a distinctive characteristic of these two vss.

Griffith

E’en humble rites with his Bay steeds he visits: he wields the bolt, drinks Soma, gives us cattle.
He makes the valiant rich in store of heroes, accepts our praise and hears the singer’s calling.

Geldner

Der Besucher so vieler Somaopfer mit seinem Falbenpaar, Tr├дger der Keule, Trinker des Soma, Schenker der K├╝he, Macher des mannhaften Helden zum Vater von lauter S├╢hnen, Erh├╢rer des Rufs der S├дngers, vom Preislied angezogen.

Grassmann

Zu schwachem Trank auch kommt er mit den F├╝chsen, den Blitz im Arm, trinkt Soma, schenket K├╝he, Versieht den tapfern Mann mit allen Helden, vernimmt den Ruf des S├дngers, Lob empfangend.

Elizarenkova

рдкреНрд░рджрд┐рд╡рдГ рдкреБрд░рд╛рдгреИрдГ рдпрдГ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ рдирдГ рдЕрд╕реНрдорджрд░реНрдердореН рдЕрдк: рдкреЛрд╖рдгрд╛рджрд┐рдХрдВ рдХрд░реНрдо рдХрдГ рдХрд░реЛрддрд┐ рдЕрдпрдорд┐рдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ рдпрддреН рд╕реНрддреЛрддреНрд░рд╛рджрд┐рдХрдВ рд╡рд╡рд╛рди рдХрд╛рдордпрддреЗ рдЕрд╕реНрдореИ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╛рдп рд╡рдпрдВ рддрджреНрд╡рд┐рд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдордГ рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкреНрдиреБрдордГ ред рдХреБрд░реНрдо рдЗрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рд╕реЛрдореЗ рд╕реБрддреЗ рдЕрднрд┐рд╖реБрддреЗ рд╕рддрд┐ рд╕реНрддреБрдорд╕рд┐ рд╕реНрддреБрдордГ ред рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╛рдп рд╕реНрддреЛрддреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐ рдХреБрд░реНрдордГред рдЙрдХреНрдерд╛ рдЙрдХреНрдерд╛рдирд┐ рд╢рд╕реНрддреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐ рд╢рдВрд╕рддреН рд╢рдВрд╕рдиреНрддрдГ ред рдкреНрд░рдердорд╛рдмрд╣реБрд╡рдЪрдирд╕реНрдп рд▓реБрдХреН ред рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдо рд╣рд╡рд┐рд░реНрд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгрдордиреНрдирдореН рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╛рдп рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╛рд░реНрдердВ рд╡рд░реНрдзрдирдВ рдпрдерд╛ рд╡реГрджреНрдзрд┐рдХрд░рдореН рдЕрд╕рддреН рд╕реНрдпрд╛рддреН рддрдерд╛ рдХреБрд░реНрдо рдЗрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ рее рее резрел рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬTo that Indra, who of old has rendered us good offices, we address (the praise) that he is plural ased by; we celebrate him when the soma is effused, repeating the prayer that the (sacrificial) food (offered) to Indra may be for his augmentation.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

It is for him that we toil at what he holds dearтАФfor Indra, who has performed labor for us from of old.
When the soma is pressed, we sing praise; (a priest) recites the
solemn words, so that the sacred formulation will be strengthening for Indra.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The first p─Бda contains an example of an embedded relative that is difficult to sidestep: in ├бsmai vay├бс╣Г y├бd v─Бv─Б╠Бna t├бd viviс╣гma the first two words dat. ├бsmai and nom. vay├бm rightly belong to the main cl. t├бd viviс╣гma тАЬwe toil at that,тАЭ which follows the dependent cl. y├бd v─Бv─Б╠Бna тАЬwhat he holds dear.тАЭ The two preposed pronouns set the participants and case roles for the vs. (see esp. ├нndr─Бya opening b and d, as well as the two 1st pl. verbs viviс╣гma and stumasi) – hence my tr. as a cleft construction – but the construction still seems unusual.

The opening of c, sut├й s├│me stumasi, takes the same elements found in the figure in vs. 1ab and plays on different phonological similarities. Here sut(├й) and stu(masi) are scrambled versions of each other, while s├│me stands somewhat apart.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬSince, Indra, you have made the (sacred) prayers (the means of) your augmentation, we address such to you, along with our praises; may we offer gratifying and acceptable eulogies to the drinker of the effused libation, with (our) sacrifices.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

For you have made the sacred formulations strengthening for yourself, to the extent that we have toiled for you, Indra, with our thoughts.
When the soma is pressed, o soma-drinker, might we make (the
pressings/the formulations) to be most wealful, enjoyable means of
increase (for you) through our sacrifices.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The first hemistich can be interpr. as a rough repair of the problematic 5a: what Indra holds dear (5a) are the formulations that he makes strengthening for himself (6a), and this is what we have toiled for (6b), with viviс╣гmaс╕е in a syntactically more orthodox position than in 5a. (6a also of course is responsive to 5d.) The phrase opening the 2nd hemistich, sut├й s├│me sutap─Б╠Бс╕е, echoes 5c, with sut(ap─Б╠Бс╕е) an anagram of stu(masi).

The referent of the acc. pl. neut. adjs. in cd is unspecified; either the pressings or the formulations – or, better, both – would work. Both are elsewhere qualified as ┼Ы├бс╣Гtama-: cf. VIII.33.15 s├бvan─Б santu ┼Ы├бс╣Гtam─Б and V.73.10 im─Б╠Бbr├бhm─Бс╣Зi v├бrdhan─Б тАж santu ┼Ы├бс╣Гtam─Б.

A rare ex. of variant readings, the hapax r─Б╠Бс╣Зdya-/r─Б╠Бndrya- is unclear. Geldner refuses to tr. it. The published translation тАШenjoyableтАЩ (which should be marked with ?) rests on HoffmannтАЩs suggestion (reported in EWA s.v. r─Б╠Бс╣Зс╕Нya-), deriving it from тИЪraс╣З (or тИЪram). Certainty of course is impossible, but some such meaning fits the context.

v├бkс╣гana- in d serves as a synonymous substitute for v├бrdhana- (5d, 6a).

Griffith

Thou hast made prayer the means of thine exalting, therefore we wait on thee with hymns, O Indra.
May we, by the pressed Soma, Somadrinker! bring thee, with sacrifice, blissful sweet refreshment.

Geldner

Denn die Kraftworte hast du zu deiner St├дrkung gemacht; solche schaffen wir dir mit unseren Gebeten. Zum gepre├Яten Soma wollen wir dir, du Somatrinker, recht zusagende ……..St├дrkungen durch Opfer bereiten.

Grassmann

Denn du hast dir Gebet erw├дhlt als Labsal, so dienen wir dir, Indra, mit Gebeten; Beim Somasafte, Somatrinker, brachten durch Opfer wir heilvolle, liebe St├дrkung.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAccept, Indra, who are condescending, our cakes and butter; drink the soma mixed with curds; sit down upon this sacred grass (strewn by) the worshipper; grant ample possessions to him who depends on you.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

As giver, take notice of our offering cake; drink the soma, foamy with cows [=milk], Indra.
Sit right here on the ritual grass of the sacrificer. Make wide, wide
space for him in devoted pursuit of you.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Note pleonastic+++(=redundant)+++ #ur├║m тАж ulok├бm#.

Griffith

Mark well our sacrificial cake, delighted Indra, drink Soma and the milk commingled.
Here on the sacrificer’s grass be seated: give ample room to thy devoted servant.

Geldner

Achte auf unseren Reiskuchen und sei freigebig; trink doch den Soma, bei dem die Milch vorschmeckt, Indra! Setz dich auf dieses Barhis des Opfernden, schaff deinem Verehrer ger├дumigen Platz!

Grassmann

Den Opferkuchen ├╝berlass uns, Indra, den milchgemischten Soma aber trinke; Auf diese Streu des Opfrers setz dich nieder und schaffe weiten Raum dem dir ergebnen.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬRejoice, fierce Indra, according to your plural asure; let these libations reach you; invoked of many, may these our invocations ascend to you; may this praise influence you for our protection.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Find elation according to your liking, mighty one. Let these sacrifices reach you.
Let these calls among us (reach) the one called by many. Might this
insightful thought guide you here for help, Indra.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As in III.41.6 (=VI.45.27) mandasv─Б is not accented despite following h├н; see comm. ad III.41.6. I have no explanation (nor does Oldenberg, despite his ref. to himself). It can be noted that in all three passages the h├н occurs in 3rd position, after the verb (all three identically s├б mandasv─Б h├н), but this position is not sufficient to explain the lack of accent, since h├н elsewhere occurs after its accented verb (e.g., I.2.4 ├нndavo v─Бm u┼Ы├бnti h├н# ; cf., e.g., I.105.18, 131.6, III.14.5, 26.8, VII.3.3, 23.5, 59.5, VIII.21.18, IX.85.2, X.30.12, 34.11). Note esp. I.189.6, IX.49.4, X.68.7, where h├н is in 3rd position after the verb as here. Since h├н often appears after initial accented verbs – for 2nd sg. med. impvs. like mandasv─Б see the numerous exx. of #yukс╣гv─Б╠Бh├н (I.10.3, etc.) – it might be possible to construct a scenario wherein when such an impv. is displaced from initial position by the pronoun s├б, it loses its accent by some sort of syntactic analogy. But I find this unlikely: RVic poets are quite sensitive to their accent rules.

P─Бda c lacks a verb, but the close parallelism of b and c (pr├б [тАж] im├й) and the semantic connection of the two nom. pl.s yaj├▒─Б╠Бsaс╕е and h├бv─Бsaс╕е impose a┼Ыnuvantu from b.

In c the 1st pl. prn. asm├й, which could be either dat. or loc., doesnтАЩt work very well as either. Geldner tr. тАЬvon uns,тАЭ which makes contextual sense but ill fits either possible case form. The published translation takes it as loc., though the tr. is awkward.

I donтАЩt know why the modal temperature has been raised, as it were, by precative yamy─Бс╕е in d – though it is the case that there are no 3rd sg. root aor. impvs. attested to тИЪyam, perhaps because a putative *yaс╣Гtu or *yantu would coincide with the much more common 3rd pl. root pres. impv. to тИЪi тАШgoтАЩ.

Griffith

O Mighty One, be joyful as thou willest. Let these our sacrifices reach and find thee;
And may this hymn and these our invocations turn thee, whom many men invoke, to help us.

Geldner

So erg├╢tze dich also nach Wohlgefallen, du Gewaltiger! Zu dir sollen diese Opfer gelangen, zu dir, dem Vielgerufenen, diese Anrufungen von uns. Dich soll dieses Gebet zur Gnade lenken, Indra!

Grassmann

Erg├╢tze dich nach Lust denn, o gewalt’ger; es m├╢gen diese Opfer dich erreichen; Dich vielgerufnen diese unsre Rufe; dich, Indra, locke dies Gebet zur H├╝lfe.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬFriends, when the libations are effused, do you satisfy that liberal Indra with the soma; let there be plural nty for him, that (he may provide) for our nourishmen; Indra never neglects the care of him who presents copious oblations.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

So that he (will be) together with you at the pressings, comrades, fill him with soma juices, Indra the benefactor.
Surely he will be there for us for the taking? Indra will not neglect the soma-presser, not neglect to help him.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Once again a dependent clause seems to follow fronted portions of the main clause, in this case t├бс╣Г vaс╕е sakh─Бyaс╕е. (Although vaс╕е sakh─Бyaс╕е could belong semantically in the dependent clause, their lack of accent requires them to follow along with t├бm, or so it seems to me.) As in 5a the fronted material seems to establish the participants in the rest of hemistich: the god and the worshipers. The acc. t├бm is then doubled by both ─лm and the real referent ├нndram in the main clause of b.

The foregoing assumes that the ellipsis of the verb in p─Бda a is not to be filled with a verb that could take t├бm as object or goal. I have in fact tried to find such a verb that an audience would supply when confronted with s├бm тАж sut├йс╣гu, but I have not been able to come up with a plausible one. The most likely verb to supply is тИЪas, esp. given 5d y├бth─Б╠Бsat, 9c ├бsati, and 10c ├бsad y├бth─Б. Geldner supplies тАЬsich erg├╢tze,тАЭ presumably a form of тИЪmad or тИЪmand, which would work contextually. But there is no positive evidence for this conjecture (unlike the three subjunctive forms of тИЪas with y├бth─Б just cited), and both roots are only marginally construed with s├бm.

Griffith

Friends, when thejuices flow, replenish duly your own, your bounteous Indra with the Soma.
Will it not aid him to support us? Indra. spares him who sheds the juice to win his favour.

Geldner

Diesen euren Freund, ihr Freunde, auf da├Я er am Safte sich erg├╢tze, f├╝llet mit Soma an, den freigebigen Indra! Gewi├Я wird er uns beistehen, um diesen Preis davonzutragen. Nicht m├╢ge es Indra verschm├дhen, dem Somapresser zu helfen.

Grassmann

Der gerne schenkt, ihn, euren Indra f├╝llet mit Soma, Freunde, wie ihr pflegt bei Opfern; Ob er wol beiwohnt dieser unsrer Spende? dem Somapresser k├╝rz er nicht den Beistand.

Elizarenkova

рдордШреЛрдирдГ рдзрдирд╡рддреЛ рд╣рд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдорддреЛ рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╕реНрдп рдХреНрд╖рдпрддреН рдИрд╢реНрд╡рд░рдГ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ рд╕реЛрдореЗ рд╕реБрддреЗ рдЕрднрд┐рд╖реБрддреЗ рд╕рддрд┐ рднрд░рджреНрд╡рд╛рдЬреЗрд╖реБ рднрд░рджреНрд╡рд╛рдЬреЗ рдордпрд┐ рдПрд╡ рдПрд╡рдореН рдЕрд╕реНрддрд╛рд╡рд┐ рд╕реНрддреБрддреЛрд╜рднреВрдд ред рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ рдЬрд░рд┐рддреНрд░реЗ рд╕реНрддреЛрддреНрд░реЗ рд╕реВрд░рд┐: рд╕рдиреНрдорд╛рд░реНрдЧреЗ рдкреНрд░реЗрд░рдХрдГ рдпрдерд╛ рдЕрд╕рддреН рднрд╡реЗрдд ред рдЙрдд рдЕрдкрд┐ рдЪ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╡рд╛рд░рд╕реНрдп рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡реИрд░реНрд╡рд░рдгреАрдпрд╕реНрдп рд░рд╛рдпрдГ рдзрдирд╕реНрдп рджрд╛рддрд╛ рдпрдерд╛ рднрд╡реЗрддреН рддрдерд╛ рдЕрд╕реНрддрд╛рд╡реАрддрд┐ рд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзрдГ ред рдЗрджрд┐рддрд┐ рджреНрд╡рдпрдВ рдкреВрд░рдгрдореН рее рее резрем рее рее реи рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThus has Indra, the lord of the opulent, been glorified by the Bha─Бradv─Бjas, upon the libation being effused, that he may be th director of his eulogist (to virtue), that Indra may be the giver of all desirable riches.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Just in this way, when the soma is pressed, Indra has been praised among the Bharadv─Бjas. Just he has power over the liberal man,
so that he [=liberal man] will be a patron to the singer. Indra is a giver of wealth that brings all desirable things.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I would slightly change the tr. of the loc. absol. to тАШhas been pressedтАЩ or тАШwas pressedтАЩ to accord better with the immediate past of the hymn-summary verb ast─Бvi.

Klein (DGRV I.442-43) interpr. magh├│naс╕е as acc. pl. (тАЬthe liberal onesтАЭ), which it could be morphologically, but тИЪkс╣гi тАШrule overтАЩ always takes the gen. (Grassmann gives one passage with supposed acc., V.37.4, but it belongs to the etymologically separate root тИЪkс╣гi тАШdwellтАЩ, and in any case in that passage I do not construe the acc. with that verb.) The ut├б in c is troubling: it does not seem to conjoin anything and it seems randomly positioned in the p─Бda. Klein groups it with a small set of passages where he thinks ut├б means тАШ(and) also, as wellтАЩ, and he suggests that it focuses on the immediately preceding word jaritr├й тАШsingerтАЩ, who will also receive patronage from Indra, in addition to the soma-presser in 9d. I find this unpersuasive, though I donтАЩt have an altogether better solution. One possibility is that we should supply the nom. sg. corresponding to gen. sg. magh├│naс╕е of b, namely *magh├бv─Б, and ut├б would conjoin this supplied noun with s┼лr├нс╕е. This would change the tr. to тАЬso that he will be (liberal [/a benefactor]) and a patron to the singer.тАЭ A slightly different solution, but still with the supplied *magh├бv─Б, would be to take ut├б as starting a new clause, with s┼лr├нс╕е qualifying Indra, yielding a tr. тАЬso that he [=the liberal mortal of b] will be (liberal) to the singer, and Indra (will be) a patron and giver of wealth тАжтАЭ Indra is called a s┼лr├н- in this Indra cycle (VI.29.5=37.5) and elsewhere. This second suggestion is probably less disruptive to the syntax than the first one, but I weakly favor the first because s┼лr├н- is more often used of human patrons than of gods.

Griffith

While Soma flowed, thus Indra hath been lauded, Ruler of nobles, mid the Bharadvajas,
That Indra may become the singer’s patron and give him wealth in every kind of treasure.

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдПрд╡) (рдЗрддреН) рдЕрдкрд┐ (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ) рдкрд░рдореИрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпрдГ (рд╕реБрддреЗ) рдирд┐рд╖реНрдкрдиреНрдиреЗрд╜рд╕реНрдорд┐рдЮреНрдЬрдЧрддрд┐ (рдЕрд╕реНрддрд╛рд╡рд┐) рд╕реНрддреВрдпрддреЗ (рд╕реЛрдореЗ) рдРрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпреЗ (рднрд░рджреНрд╡рд╛рдЬреЗрд╖реБ) рдзреГрддрд╡рд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдиреЗрд╖реБ (рдХреНрд╖рдпрддреН) рдирд┐рд╡рд╕реЗрддреН (рдЗрддреН) рдЕрдкрд┐ (рдордШреЛрдирдГ) рдзрдирд╛рдвреНрдпрд╛рдиреН (рдЕрд╕рддреН) рднрд╡реЗрддреН (рдпрдерд╛) (рдЬрд░рд┐рддреНрд░реЗ) рд╕реНрддрд╛рд╡рдХрд╛рдп (рдЙрдд) рдЕрдкрд┐ (рд╕реВрд░рд┐рдГ) рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдГ) (рд░рд╛рдпрдГ) рдзрдирд╕реНрдп (рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╡рд╛рд░рд╕реНрдп) рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡реЗ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЗ рд╡рд╛рд░рд╛ рд╕реНрд╡реАрдХрд╛рд░рд╛ рдпрд╕реНрдорд┐рдВрд╕реНрддрд╕реНрдп (рджрд╛рддрд╛) реерезрежрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЕрддреНрд░реЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░рдГ ред рдпреЗ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛ рдЕрд╕реНрдорд┐рдЮреНрдЬрдЧрддрд┐ рдзрд░реНрдореНрдпрд╛рдгрд┐ рдХрд░реНрдорд╛рдгрд┐ рдХреБрд░реНрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ рддреЗ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рджрд╛ рд╕реНрддреВрдпрдиреНрддреЗ рдпрдерд╛ рджрд╛рдирдВ рдкреНрд░рд┐рдпрдХрд╛рд░рдХрдВ рднрд╡рддрд┐ рддрдерд╛ рд╣реНрдпрд╛рджрд╛рдирдВ рди рднрд╡рддреАрддрд┐ реерезрежрее рдЕрддреНрд░реЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рджреНрд░рд╛рдЬрдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдЧреБрдгрд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░реНрд╡реЗрджреНрдпрд╛ рее рдЗрддреНрдпреГрдЧреНрд╡реЗрджрднрд╛рд╖реНрдпреЗ рд╖рд╖реНрдареЗ рдордгреНрдбрд▓реЗ рджреНрд╡рд┐рддреАрдпреЛрд╜рдиреБрд╡рд╛рдХрд╕реНрддреНрд░рдпреЛрд╡рд┐рдВрд╢рдВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рд╖реЛрдбрд╢реЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдпрд╛ рдордВрддреНрд░рд╛рдд рдЙрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдВрдХрд╛рд░ рдЖрд╣реЗ. рдЬреА рдорд╛рдгрд╕реЗ рдзрд░реНрдордпреБрдХреНрдд рдХрд░реНрдо рдХрд░рддрд╛рдд рддреНрдпрд╛рдВрдЪреА рд╕реНрддреБрддреА рд╣реЛрддреЗ. рдЬрд╕реЗ рджрд╛рди рджреЗрдгреЗ рдкреНрд░рд┐рдп рдЕрд╕рддреЗ рддрд╕реЗ рджрд╛рди рдШреЗрдгреЗ рдкреНрд░рд┐рдп рдирд╕рддреЗ. рее резреж рее
